GT Equivalence Verification (BPG22)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - exp(-c2*P))*P + c3*P*exp(-c4*t)
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can be made equivalent to the GT:

$$GT = 0.11782(1 - e^{-0.02723P})P + 0.11782 P e^{-0.02723t}$$

Expanding: $GT = 0.11782P - 0.11782P e^{-0.02723P} + 0.11782P e^{-0.02723t}$

The key structural features are:
1. A term linear in P: $aP$
2. A term $-aP e^{-bP}$ (P times exponential in P)
3. A term $aP e^{-bt}$ (P times exponential in t)

Let me check candidates that have both $P \cdot \exp(t)$ terms and $P \cdot \exp(P)$ terms.

**Candidate 23**: $P c_0 \exp(c_1 t) + c_2 + c_3 \exp(c_4 t) + c_5 \log(c_6 \exp(P c_7) + 1) + c_8 \exp(P c_9)$

This has $P \exp(c_1 t)$ which can give $P e^{-bt}$. It has $\log(c_6 \exp(Pc_7) + 1)$ and $\exp(Pc_9)$. But I need $-P e^{-bP}$ which is hard to get from log or exp terms alone.

**Candidate 15**: $P c_0 + P c_1 \exp(c_2 t) + P c_3 \log(P c_4 + 1) + c_5 + c_6 \exp(P c_7) \exp(c_8 t)$

This has $P \log(Pc_4+1)$ not $Pe^{-P}$.

**Candidate 22**: $P c_0 + P c_1 + P c_2 \log(P c_3 + 1) + c_4 + c_5 \exp(c_6 t) + c_7 \exp(P c_8)$

The GT term $-0.11782 P e^{-0.02723P}$ is not a pure exponential in P (it's P times exponential). $c_7 \exp(Pc_8)$ can't produce $P \exp(P \cdot \text{const})$.

**Candidate 40**: $P c_0 \exp(c_1 t) + P c_2 + P^{c_3} c_4 t^{c_5} + c_6 \exp(c_7 t) + c_8/P^5$

Setting $c_5 = 0$: $P^{c_3} c_4$ ŌĆö this gives a power of P, not $P e^{-bP}$.

**Candidate 17**: $P c_0 \exp(P c_1) + c_2 \exp(c_3 t) + c_4 + c_5 \sin(c_6 \log(P c_7 + 1) + c_8)$

This has $P \exp(Pc_1)$! Setting $c_1 = -0.02723$ gives $P e^{-0.02723P}$. Then I need $c_2 \exp(c_3 t)$ for the time-dependent part... but the GT has $P \exp(-bt)$, not just $\exp(-bt)$.

So $c_2 \exp(c_3 t)$ can't produce $P \exp(-bt)$.

**Candidate 25**: $P c_0 \exp(P c_1) + P^{c_2} c_3 + c_4 t^2 + c_5 \exp(c_6 t) + c_7 t + c_8 t^2$

Has $P \exp(Pc_1)$ and $P^{c_2} c_3$, but no $P \exp(t)$ term.

**Candidate 1**: $P c_0 + P c_1 \exp(c_2 t) + c_3 + c_4 \sin(c_5 + c_6 \log(P c_7 + 1))$

This has $P \exp(c_2 t)$ for the time part. But $\sin(c_5 + c_6 \log(Pc_7+1))$ needs to produce $-P e^{-bP}$, which it cannot since sin of log can't produce $Pe^{-bP}$.

After thorough analysis, none of the candidates contain both $P \cdot \exp(\text{const} \cdot P)$ and $P \cdot \exp(\text{const} \cdot t)$ terms simultaneously, which are required by the GT.

[NO MATCH]

### Candidate 32: `P*c0*exp(c1*t) + P*c2/(P + c3) + c4*t**2 + c5*t + c6 + c7*t*log(P*c8 + 1)`

`t*log(cP+1)` mixes P and t. Setting c7=0: rational in P, can't match.

### Candidate 37: `P*c0*exp(c1*t) + P*c2/(P + c3) + c4*t**2 + c5*t + c6 + c7*log(c8*exp(P*c9) + 1)`

Has `P*exp(ct)` Ō£ō. `log(c8*exp(cP)+1)`: for c9<0 and large P, this ŌåÆ log(c8┬Ę0+1) = 0; for P=0, log(c8+1). This is like a softplus. Not `P*exp(-cP)`.

Actually, let me reconsider. GT = `c0*P - c0*P*exp(-c2*P) + c3*P*exp(-c4*t)`.

`log(c8*exp(c9*P)+1)` with c9<0: this is `log(c8*exp(-|c9|P)+1)`. For small P: Ōēł log(c8+1). For large P: Ōēł 0. This doesn't have the right shape (GT's P-dependent part grows linearly).

Candidate 37 verdict: [NO MATCH]
